Currently, Shanghai No. 1 produces PVC gloves three shifts a day because of high
market demand. These gloves are popular in the chemical, electroplating, machinery
manufacturing, construction, and fishing industries.
The results of the project were recognized by the plant's Japanese partner. A joint
venture was established in 1996, and the production of gloves was further expanded.
Furthermore, gloves from the plant have been included in the "Shanghai New Products
Program." 97 percent of the products are exported to Japan, the United States, and
Canada. Demand is still increasing due to the growing economy and increased
enforcement of safety regulations. The: 1997 mission advised the factory to expand its
product base for long-term sustainability.
B-05-SHA   Shanghai Yi Er Bao Lactic Acid Products Factory
Through this project, Shanghai Yi Er Bao Lactic Acid Factory (Shanghai Lactic
Acid) has built a lactic acid production line with an annual capacity of 1,500 tons. The
technology was supplied by Shanghai Industrial Microbiology Research Institute
(SIMRI).
Lactic acid is an important chemical used in the food, pharmaceutical, and
chemical industries. Research and development of lactic acid production is one of the key
programs included in China's eighth "Five Year Plan." China had been importing
industrial lactic acid before the start up of the production line in the factory. SIMRI's
success in this program has enabled Clhina to have its own lactic acid production. It has
also initiated more R & D into applications of advance microbiological technologies in
"downstream" industries as food, pharmaceutical, and chemical production in both the
Spark Intensive Area (Qian Wen Village) where the project is located, and in the
Shanghai area.
The production of lactic acid in Shanghai started in 1996. Currently, both
production and quality are stable. A Dutch company has signed a letter of intent for a
possible joint venture with Shanghai Lactic Acid after several site studies. This project
should further develop the applications of lactic acid.
B-17 JEDI Dunhua Hua Kang Pharmaceutical Factory
Through the project, Hua Kang has improved its production line to produce
traditional Chinese medicines for heart disease. Proper design of the medicine and more
accurate market forecasts have made product sales very good. Sales in 1997 totaled Y 200
million, 200 times more than in 1993.
The medicine is well recognized in China because of its effectiveness in treating
heart problems and its quality. This effectiveness and quality was made possible by the
utilization of advanced pharmaceulical technologies and scientific management
techniques that Hua Kang has gained through this project.

The development of the factory also has had a positive influence on the local
economy. The sales of the printing, pulp and paper, raw materials, glass, packaging,
advertising, food, and tourism industries increased Y 40 million in 1997.
B-21-JEDI Siping Hongzui Machinery General Plant
Siping Hongzui is one of the largest TVEs in China. It imported advanced
technologies and equipment for rolling and casting from the United States in 1995. The
total investment is Y 110 million, including Y 21.2 million from the World Bank.
Production reached full capacity in May 1997. Hongzui has repaid Y 4.19 million to the
Bank so far.
The rolling and casting machines that Siping Hongzui is manufacturing are the
most advanced in China. Siping Hongzui has disseminated this technology successfully
to its customers. It helped Jiangxi Suichang Steel General Plant design and manufacture
four rolling and casting machines. Sales in 1996 totaled Y 16 million. Profit before tax
was Y 5 million.



- 62-                    APPENDIX B
APPENDIX B: BORROWER'S CONTRIBUTION TO THE ICR
BACKGROUND
1.   In China in middle 1980, the Spark Program for invigoration of rural economy
relying on science and technology had supported the development of township and
village enterprises, promoted the rural economy, and achieved remarkable successes; and
thus enjoyed universal recognition and great popularity among the people. With the
development of economic refornation, township and village enterprises have become one
of the important constituents of national economy and an momentous force promoting the
steady progress of market-oriented economy of China.
2.    The progressive establishment of market-oriented economy faces severe
challenges from strategic change of a rapidly growing economy into a profit-making one
as well as from an extensive economy into an intensive one. The continuation of the
reform and open policies call for the further development of the Spark Program in order
to assist the steady, fast and healthy growth of the township and village enterprises.
3.    The Spark Program will find a vast space for its further development by
utilization of foreign capital. The State Science and Technology Commission (SSTC) has
timely formulated the strategy for further expansion of the Spark Program using the loans
from the World Bank.
4.    At the same time, the Spark Program and its far-reaching influence on the
progress in the developing countries had won the attention of the World Bank.
Consequently, four delegations dispatched by the World Bank had investigated and
evaluated the Program, and concluded with a appraisal report in 1989.
5.    Owing to the joint efforts of the SSTC, the State Planning Commission, Ministry
of Finance, and the World Bank, a agreement of utilization of the loan from the World
Bank for the Spark Program duly came into effect on June 14, 1991.
6.    Three areas selected for the trial run of the Program were Jiangsu Province, Jilin
Province and Chongming County in Shanghai. For these three areas, two in the south and
one in the north of China, each has its own representative feature. Jiangsu Province lies in
a coastal area of relatively highly developed economy, where China township and village
enterprises grow rapidly and vigorously in terms of quantity, scale, technology as well as
managerial levels. Actually, the southern part of Jiangsu is the birthplace of China
township and village enterprises. Jilin Province is one of the important bases of the
national fundamental and processing industries in addition to a principal cereal-producing
area. However, its rural industry lags clue to the late starting up of township and village
enterprises. Accordingly, the advantages of resources there have not been sufficiently



-63 -                   APPENDIX B
made use of. Chongming county is an alluvial island in the mouth of Yangtze River with
potential of being in economically superior position, but its development had been
hindered by the lack of transportation facilities. The purpose of selection of these three
areas for the trial implementation of the Spark Program using the loan from World Bank
is to enhance the demonstration effect as much as possible.
PROJECT OBJECTIVES
7.    The objectives of this Project is to explore ways of and acquire experience in
utilization of international capitals, to open up more sources of funds for the Program,
and to promote the matching up of the practice and market of the Program to those
prevailing internationally by means of introduction of loan from the World Bank.
Moreover, it is to make demonstrations in the three areas representing different
characteristic conditions to support the steady growth of industry and the upgrading of
technology so as to improve the efficiency, product quality as well as the environment in
rural industry. Furthermore, as the key point, it is to adjust the rural economic structure,
to improve the township enterprises, and to realize the rural modernization. Even more
important, it is to acquire advanced experience through organization of the
implementation of the Program using the loan from the World Bank to secure highly
evolved management so as to construct for the Program a model of management meeting
the new economic situation as well as the standard market oriented economy, and,
moreover, to train staff to serve competently the further development of the Program.
8.    For this purpose, World Bank provided a total amount of loan equivalent to
US$114.3 million, 90 percent of which was used to support the development of
subprojects of township and village enterprises, and other 10 percent interest-free soft
loan was used to support the technology for upgrading of management, including
establishment of training demonstration bases, technical information system, and the
training of staff in technological appraisal and its methodology.
9.    The disbursement of the loan comprised US$65 million to Jiangsu Province,
US$25 million to Jilin Province, and US$20 million to Chongming County of Shanghai
municipality. In addition, 243 million Japanese yen from Japanese Government Grant
support Technical Assistance Components implementation at state level.
PROJECT DESCRIPTION
10.   The objectives of the Project itself constitute the important parts of the contents,
which may be divided into four subprograms of A, B, C and D as follows:
(a) Subcomponent A is an industrialization one consisting of two components of:
(i) Commercial subprojects, which supported the township and village
enterprises (plus limited number of collective enterprises affiliated to a
county) to undertake technologically matured commercial subprojects.



-64 -                    APPENDIX B
(ii) Precommercial subprojects, which supported the technologically developing
products  or  processes  in  Jiangsu  Province  before  their  full
commercialization.
(b) Subcomponents B, C and D are technical assistance.
11.   The subcomponent B is Spark training, which consist of training and technical
assistance. It is, through the training of managerial and technological staff and the
providing of the equipment as well as information consultation, to create advantageous
conditions for the improvement of the capacity of training, and also for upgrading the
managerial and training techniques. It is emphasized on the establishment of four key
Spark training bases located in Nanjing, Changchun, Jiangyin and Chongming in order to
make them models of high grade training base in respective areas from a start point of
high level. Also, a report on the demand for training of the Spark Program is to be
prepared for this subcomponent.
12.   The subcomponent C is a technology information system, which is oriented to
strengthening of the Institute of Scientific and Technological Information of China
(ISTIC) and information institutes of subproject area level. It is to be provided with
technical support, training and equipment in order to develop new databases, computers
and other information systems as well as establishment of networks in the subprojects
areas. This is a system of information and consultation service, which containing all
aspects of scientific and technological achievements, products, processes, marketing,
management well as sales, while focusing on township and village enterprises.
13.   The subcomponent D is establishment of organizations, which falls into two parts:
(a) The establishment of Spark plan management systems at state and provincial levels
would supply accurate, timely and full information on the establishment,
implementation, finance and achievements of the Spark subprojects to all the
managerial staff in Spark Program of different levels.
(b) The training of technical appraisal consists of preparation of a manual of standard
methods for the appraisal and management of potential projects related to the Spark
Program . It will introduce a programmed and standardized model of procedure for
the management of spark plans. M[eanwhile, it also includes the training of the staff
of relending in financial departments to carry out the management of commercial
bank, appraisal of subprojects, and management in general.
Japanese Grant Facility
14.   Besides the subcomponents A, B, and C mentioned above, there is some extra
fund accrued due to the appreciation of Japanese yen. Based on this fund, it was also
planned to accomplish 7 new subprojects of further development of consultation services,
demonstration of consultation, appraisal of Spark Program, and three case studies of the



-65 -                    APPENDIX B
areas of high density of Spark subprojects and manufacture of multimedia teaching
package.
ACHIEVEMENT OF PROJECT OBJECTIVES
Organization and Management
15.   The implementation of the Spark Subcomponent is a systematic engineering of
many layers, multiple disciplines, involving various industries and different
administrative agencies. It is a kind of highly comprehensive economic task, which was
participated by various Chinese departments of ministry level, including SSTC, the State
Planning Commission, the Ministry of Finance, financial entities, and audit bodies,
which, predominantly SSTC, Ministry of Finance, and financial intermediaries undertook
all the tasks of selection, approval, implementation, management and supervision of the
subprojects. In order to strengthen the leadership and administration of the
Subcomponent, a leading group and Spark Program office (SPO) were established in
SSTC, and corresponding leading groups and SPOs were set up in Jiangsu province, Jilin
province and Shanghai municipality, too.
16.   The Spark subprojects were implemented enthusiastically by concerted efforts of
all relevant participants led by Scientific and Technological Commissions (STC) of
different levels.
17.   STCs of different levels were the main driving force in the implementation of the
Subcomponent, which, in conformity with the goal of Spark Subcomponent, were in
charge of the organization and coordination of the planning, selection, approval,
supervision, inspection, check and acceptance of subprojects. They were responsible for
maintaining of high content of science and technology in the subprojects by means of
guidance, coordination and provision of service for all the participants.
18.   Financial organizations were the principal body of financial management that
were responsible for the drawing and onlending of the loans; management of the special
appropriation accounts; disbursement and complementation; verification of debts;
supervision of subprojects finance; and timely payment of principles, interests and fees to
authorities of different levels;
19.   The financial intermediaries were the main body of projects implementation. They
assessed independently and examined strictly the eligibility of the subprojects submitted
by enterprises, and were accountable for the granting recovery of the World Bank loan as
well as for the timely collection of commitment fee, interests and principles from
enterprises. They were also responsible for payments of principal, interest, fee, and a
certain proportion of capital for mating projects.
20.   During the practical implementation, the whole process of the projects were
guided, administrated, supervised, coordinated and served. Regulations, clear-cut
sectionalization of work, and methods of operation were formulated. For examples, there



- 66 -                   APPENDIX B
were definite and sectionalized standards of selection of enterprises and subprojects, as
well as strict examination of the establishment and appraisal of the subprojects. Both the
analysis of projects before their finalization, and the supervision in the stage of
implementation and appraisal of the completion of the projects were emphasized. An
efficient operation mechanism was established, too.
Implementation of Industrial Subprojects
Selection of Subprojects
21.  In the three areas, altogether 108 industrial subprojects were approved by the
World Bank. Among them, 63 are located in Jiangsu province (47 commercial and 16
precommercial subprojects), 29 in Jilin province, and 16 in Chongming county in
Shanghai All these subprojects were selected from hundreds candidates involving various
sectors of materials, electronics, machinery, textile, light industries, etc. 83 subprojects
were undertaken by township and village enterprises and accounted for 77 percent of the
total; 25 subprojects by collective eniterprises of county level and accounted for 23
percent. Of the 108 enterprises, 22 were newly established and 86 reformed
technologically of originally existing ones. (Table 6)
Appraisal
22.   The financial intermediaries, namely, Jiangsu Agricultural Bank, China
Investment Bank, Shanghai Agricultural Bank and Jilin Province Trust and Investment
Co., were responsible for the appraisal of all the industrial subprojects.
23.   The applied eligibility criteria of appraisal were The Standards of Qualification of
Investing Enterprises and The Standards of Qualification of Invested Projects stipulated
in Projects Agreement and The Terms and Conditions of Loaning to Subprograms
stipulated in Onlending Agreement.
Disbursement
24.   From the first drawing in October of 1991 to the last one in September of 1997,
the World Bank actually had paid US$102 million (Table 1).
Design, Tender and Purchase
25.   Under the guidance and supervision of local financial agencies and STCs, the
subprojects enterprises called for tenders for the purchase of equipment and civil
construction in confonnity with the requirements of the subproject design. The purchase
was carried out on principle of "Compare vendor offers before buying." The procedure of
design, tender and purchase had ensured the quality of the equipment, reasonableness of
price, and time of delivery.



-67 -                    APPENDIX B
Investment
26.   Based on the appraisal report of subprojects, the total amount of the planned
investment of the 108 subprojects was Y 2.08 billion, in which 48 percent came from the
World Bank and 52 percent from domestic companions of financial relending agencies
(Table 2A) . The total amount of actual investment of Y 2.15 billion, in which 47 percent
was from the World Bank, and the rest was mainly from domestic companions of
financial relending agencies, other banks, and enterprises themselves (Table 2) had
substantially supported the early start of the projects.
Results
27.   As of today, all the 108 subprojects had committed and been in good order. The
total amount of fund drawn from the World Bank was US$105 million, in which
US$3.968 million was spent by 16 precommercial subprojects. 89 subprojects had been
put into operation and accounted for 82 percent of the total hard loani; 61 subprojects had
been completed and accepted at a completeness rate of 51.2 percent; 11 subprojects were
under construction; and 8 subprojects had not been completed on schedule.
(a) From the view of the implementation of industrial subprojects, the subprojects
developed were not in balance and may be classified into following three categories:
The first category is good subprojects, which account for 38 percent of the total
subprojects. These kind of project had reached the production capacity of the design,
operated in a higher managerial level on the whole (including production, finance,
sales, and personnel), held well-opened selling channels, maintained promising
market of their products, had strong solvency, and well operated. Such as: Jilin
Huakang Pharmacy, Shanghai Chongming Polypropylene High Tenacity Fibers
Plant, Jiangsu Taixing Glass Ware Factory, etc.
The second category is common subprojects, which accounted for 39 percent of the
total. These subprojects were operated well in all internal aspects of their own;
however, owing to cost increasing resulted from the drastically going up of prices of
the raw materials, their marketing momentum gradually weakened, their account
receivable and payable increased, their circulating fund decreased immensely due to
the policy of tightening credit; their regular operation was unable to maintain
because of lacking of timely complement of capital; hence, at present time, these
enterprises were in an unsatisfactory situation of just making even or making not
much profit. The development of all these potential enterprises was constrained by
various factors. Once these constraints are released, their productivity and profits
will increase enormously. Examples of this category are: Jilin Gongzhuling
Automobile Decoration Materials Plant, Shanghai Chongming PET Sheets Plant,
and Jiangsu Changzhou Synthetic Fibers Plant No. 2, etc.
The third category is the subprojects with difficulties, which accounted for 23
percent of the total. Owing to the failure of passing on of the capital for mating



-68 -                    APPENDIX B
components, prolongation of the construction duration, change of market, product
problems, poor management of enterprises, suffering from natural calamities,
technology and equipment being too advanced to operate, products being too
advanced to meet the demand, poor technology, lack of competent technical workers,
.... and others, these subprojects were unable to operate well; and, therefore, it led to
their profit decreasing, being unable to reach the desired benefit, increasing burden,
suffering loss, and even stop or being close to stop of operation.
(b) All the 10 precommercial subprojects in the first phase of implementation had been
completed, and other 6 subprojects had been approved by the World Bank in early
1996 and were proceeding well umder implementation. In view of the situation of
implementation, all the subprojects basically were successful. It is anticipated that
about 50 percent of the subprojects would become commercial subprojects. The
precommercial subprojects belonged to development activities of higher technology.
Based on the survey and analysis, most of the technological introduction were those
having passed the tests of laboratory experiments and small scale pilot production,
accounting for 60 percent; those having passed the examinations of medium scale
pilot plant production or large scale plant production, accounting for 40 percent.
From the point of view of technology, 40 percent of the precommercial subprojects
had not much development activil:ies in science and technology, and, hence, there is
a certain distance from what was required by the World Bank.
(c) Thanks to the demanding regulations of examination for environmental reports,
satisfactory achievements with respect to the environment had been made. There is
no problem of environmental po]llution with all the subprojects of Spark Program
supported by the World Bank.
Profits
28.   Between 1992 and 1996, the 79 subprojects in operation created profits plus tax
amounting to Y 236 million, in which Y 129 million came from Jiangsu, Y 97 million
from Jilin, and Y 10 million from Shanghai. 13,600 employment of rural labors were
made through the implementation of these subprojects.
Repayment of Capital with Interest
29.   By the end of December 1996, the sum of accrued interest was US$14.38 million,
of which US$4.91 million or 34.1 percent had been repaid (Table 4); the Up to end June
of 1997, sum of accumulated principle: was US$61.67 million, of which US$14.7 million
had been extended and US$22.49 million had been repaid. Some of the subprojects were
put into operation and brought profits late because of their delayed investment. Others
had been poorly operated with the problems of lack of legal sense. Therefore, it is
difficult for them to repay fully the capital with interest at the present time. The financial
relending agencies were making efforts to collect the loans, and for some of the projects,
the terms of contracts had been extended based on their concrete conditions (Table 5).



- 69-                    APPENDIX B
TRAINING AND TECHNICAL ASSISTANCE
30.   The training and technical assistance of Spark Project are unique.
31.   Big Sum. The whole technical assistance used US$9.50 million or accounted for
about 1/10 of the total loan from the World Bank.
32.   Complicated Content of Projects. It included the training, technical information,
managerial information and subproject appraisal for the three big constituents of the first
design. In the expenditures, it included also building construction, equipment purchasing,
consultation and training. Lately, it elaborately planned 7 new subprojects, in accordance
with the targets designed originally, utilizing the US$0.60 million accrued from the
appreciation of Japanese yen. Altogether, 15 agreements of technical assistance and
consultation were signed (Table 14).
33.  Involving All Aspects. The objective of the training and technical assistance of
Spark Project was to upgrade the overall managerial level, and thus all aspects of the
Project were involved in.
-  Broad Range of Technical Disciplines. Including techniques of training, computer
information, financial appraisal, systematic engineering, consultation, management,
etc.
*  Participants from Widespread Sectors. Including 15 consultation firms of bid
winners for subproject implementation, about dozen of departments from SSTC,
trainees from Jiangsu, Jilin, Shanghai and managerial and relevant people of Spark
Program from other 30 provinces and municipalities. The total numbers of them were
about 75 organizations and 850 people.
* Long Duration. The duration of the activities for training and technical assistance
was about 5 years from 1992 to the end of December of 1996.
34.   Fruitfulness. The extensive activities of training and technical assistance were
elaborately organized and earnestly implemented by SSTC, and were fully and
successfully completed in accordance with the agreements. The achievements were
universally recognized by people. 54 training courses were given and 2,100 person-time
were trained (Table 10 and 11), 4 modem training bases were established (Nanjing,
Jiangyin, Chongming, and Changchun), modem equipment of a value of about US$5.53
million was installed in the training bases for the information institutes and managerial
agencies related to the Spark Program (Table 13). These training bases had become the
key or demonstration ones of the Spark Program in the state or provinces. The
information institutes at all levels of state, province, municipality, and county had
enthusiastically provided the township and village enterprises as well as governments of
different levels with information in the form of computers, publications, videos and
others. Among them, 50 consultation reports and 36 text books were accomplished. Four
of the text books had been published; 8 information and database management systems
had been established; and 5 Instruction packages had been completed (Table 11). Based



- 70-                    APPENDIX B
on the achievements of some of the above mentioned subprojects as well as the
subsequent demonstration consultation projects and three project cases, the real problems
in Spark Program and the development of enterprises had been solved in a way of
integrating theory with practice. For examples, the development strategy for Yiyang
urban area in Hunan province, the marketing and management of Jiangyin Steel Cable
Plant, and the appraisal of the area of dense Spark projects had won widespread acclaim
in all managerial departments of Spark Program, and, thus, contributed to the experience
in how to serve the township and village enterprises for the consultation business in
China.
35.   Great Influence. The physical achievements of training and technical assistance
projects were obvious, and their intangible influence on the Spark Program, the progress
of science and technology, and the development of rural industry was even deeper and
farther. The contents of the subprojects met the requirement of the transformation of
planned economy into socialist market economy in China. In recent years, Chinese
government had taken a series of measures in order to reform the systems of finance,
taxation, investment, and governmental functions. In order to fit in with the new
conditions, the major supporting factors of the Spark Program were changing from the
fund and preferential policies into technology, information and management. The training
and technical assistance activities of the Program had educated a great number of
professional people of new thought and skills, created new models of management and
new information systems, and promoted the development of Chinese consultation
business. All of them had strengthened the ability of scientific and technological services
and laid the foundation of operation of Spark Program in market economy.
IMPLEMENTATION IRECORD AND MAJOR FACTORS
AFFECT'ING THE PROJECT
36.   During the 6 years of implemenltation, the Program Leading Group of SSTC had
held 7 working conferences and worked out timely the direction and focal tasks in
accordance with the existing situation at that time.
37.  In the starting phase, the principle of "Use the money early, adequately, and
properly" was proposed to lead the projects from preparative work to formal
implementation.
38.  In the implementation phase, the method of "Simplify it, prepay it, subsidize it"
was proposed in order to promote the uttilization of the loan and expedite the progress of
the projects.
39.  In the light of the requirements of the Spark Program, that the Spark subprojects
should be of "High profits, high grade, high exemplary" was proposed so as to gradually
lead the projects using the loan from the World Bank to subprojects of large scale,
application of high technology and location mainly on the area where Spark subprojects
were aggregated.



-71-                     APPENDIX B
40.  In order to promote the repetitive utilization of the loan from the World Bank, the
new target of "Pay attention to management, increase profits, grasp firmly the repayment
of the loan, promote development" was set to arrange the key activities in the coming
period.
Schedule
1986-89                The phase of preparation before start of the projects.
1989-Jun 1991          The phase of negotiation of the projects.
Jun 1991- Sep 1997      The phase of implementation of the projects.
Sep 30, 1997           Deadline of drawing of the loan (The former one was
September 30, 1996)
Jun 1997               The phase for projects post-evaluation.
41.   Actually, the phase of implementation of the projects was delayed for one year.
Therefore, SSTC applied for the postponement of deadline for drawing the loan, which
was then changed into September 30 of 1997.
Changes of Important Policies
42.   Foreign Currency. In 1994, the concurrent existence of two systems of foreign
exchange rate became the single system of market foreign exchange rate. It led to the
change of the components and cost of the investment in Renminbi.
43.   Commodity Price. In 1993 the coexistence of planned and market economies in
China was changed into only one system of market economy. And, hence, all the prices
involved in the Spark subprojects were determined by the market.
44.   Finance. The government changed original professional banks, including China
Agricultural Bank, into commercial banks. And, consequently, the alteration of the credit
policy of intermediary financial bodies was induced.
45.   Taxation. The repayment of the loan before taxation was replaced by repayment
of the loan after taxation.
46.   The delay of loaned Spark Program implementation for one year was mainly due
to:
(a) It lacked of appraisal experience for the World Bank loaned projects in first
implementation phase. The financial intermediaries were entitled to simplify the
appraisal of free quota as late as in 1993. Hence, the efficiency was kept so low that
most of the subprojects were to be approved in a short period of 1993-94.
(b) Disbursement and replenishment did not work smoothly or replenishment was made
slowly, and, therefore, the construction and the fund circulation of subprojects were
affected.



- 72 -                    APPENDIX B
(c) Domestic counterpart fund was unreliable, and the starting fund was inadequate and
the financing and fund flowing did not catch up to some extent.
(d) The time schedule of subproject appraisal did not have enough leeway. For instance,
Jilin did not take account of the cold weather affecting the construction and,
therefore, did not extend properly the deadline of construction completion.
47.   Although most of the subprojects were completed and went into operation, their
profits did not hit the targets initially desired. The major reasons are as follows:
(a) Too high productivity was predicted at the appraisal of the subprojects. In fact, in the
productivity, technology, finance, and others were more complicated than those
thought before, and, consequently, a relatively big difference from those desired
initially was formed.
(b) Owing to the changes of prices and exchange rates, the investment budgets were
overspent, the cost increased, and the overall profits decreased.
(c) The scarcity of working capital and failure of clearing up of debt chain caused some
of the subprojects unable to maintain their normal production.
(d) Some of the projects with unmatured technology or not well-tested processes,
poor internal management, inadeiquate technical personnel, and insufficient
ability for persistent development had led the enterprise profits going steadily
downhill.
PROJECTS SUSTAINABILITY
48.   In the view of future development, the hard Spark loan from the World Bank for
the subprojects satisfied the requirements of adjustment of industry directions and the
environmental policies of China. The subprojects supported by the loan from the World
Bank had high quality of technology, Based on the results. of sampling analysis, 80
percent of the subprojects reached the advanced domestic level, in which 19.35 percent
were of worldwide leading technology. Most of the subprojects started from
technological levels sharply more advanced than other industrial projects; accordingly,
they possessed the ability for further development on their own.
49.   Most of the enterprises that sponsored the subprojects have good capacity to
maintain their technology at high level. In the point of view of technical input, each
subproject had recruited 21 technical people on average. Thus, the enterprises had
introduced technical human resource, trained a number of technical people, as well as
made their progress in technology. For the commercial subprojects, the investment in the
equipment, technology experimentation and training accounted for 60-70 percent of the
total investment Therefore, the subprojects were of good sustainability with respect to
their technical efficiency.



- 73 -                   APPENDIX B
50.   The World Bank subprojects emphasized on the promotion of newly developed
industries of materials, electronics, information, and machinery as well as those of
industrial equipment and accessory products used for large scale plants. It cultivated the
growing points of economy. Its strategy conformed to the trend of economic development
and, therefore, increased the competitiveness in the market. The construction scale and
degree of modernization of a considerable number of the World Bank subprojects were
bigger and higher than those of the ordinary sole domestic Spark projects for
development of science and technology. For this reason, these enterprises should have
strong competitive capacity.
51.   Consequently, as a whole, most of the subprojects have broad prospects and are
able to further develop continually.
BANK PERFORMANCE
52.   The support of the World Bank raised the position of Spark Program and
enhanced its influence internationally. And the fact that the World Bank highly appraised
the spirit of dedication and creation of the officers of SSTC further encouraged them in
their work.
53.   The World Bank paid much attention to the role of financial intermediary
institutions, and provided them with necessary guidance and training in the management
of the loan, manipulation of fund, and assessment of subprojects. It helped their staff to
master quickly the international financing in large scale as well as the management of the
loan from the World Bank for Spark Program.
54.  In regarding to the technical assistance, such as staff training, consultation service,
preparation of Instruction Packages, and setup of information systems, the World Bank
had paid most attention to and strongly supported it. The World Bank also offered
valuable suggestions for the diffusion of the achievements of the technical assistance
projects.
55.   The World Bank thought highly about the environmental protection and the
creation of employment for labors.
56.   The World Bank paid great attention to the diffusion of the Spark subprojects
technologies, as well as supported enthusiastically the project of "Marching to the West."
57.   The rigorous, conscientious, careful, and painstaking attitude of the officers of the
World Bank in their work in China as well as their high efficiency and quality were
inspiring and made an excellent demonstration for the managerial staff of Spark Program.
BORROWER PERFORMANCE
58.   The local STCs, financial organizations and intermediaries, and relevant agencies
of different levels had well done their duty to the implementation and supervision of the



-74-                     APPENDIX B
Program. It was their efficient efforts in the selection, preparation, assessment, and
supervision of the subprojects that made the Program proceed smoothly.
59.   The borrowers had paid much attention to the introduction of advanced
managerial techniques from the World Bank, which played an important role in the
structure adjustment of the assets of bank credit, expansion of the source of foreign long-
term loan, growth of profit, learning of the managerial experience from foreign banks,
training of modernized managerial staff, and upgrading of human resource. All of these
had promoted the improvement of the management of bank credit and given impetus to
the development of international services of the banks.
60.   The STCs of different levels took seriously of the organization and coordination
for the technical assistance. The successive completion and start of operation of the "soft"
loaned subprojects of Spark training system, management information system,
technology information system, engineering and technology evaluation system, had
facilitated the configuration of soft and hard conditions, strengthened the infrastructure of
science and technology, enhanced the capability of comprehensive service in science and
technology, created favorable conditions for further growth and sustenance of science and
technology.
ASSESSMENT OF OUTCOME
61.   The projects using the loan frorn the World Bank had explored and found a way
for funding the Spark Program internationally. The projects had constituted a situation for
healthy progress in the future. Basically, all the projects were successful due to:
(a) The target of the World Bank projects basically fitted the practical situation of rural
economy as well as the prospect and reformation of economy in China
(b) The managerial system of the World Bank projects essentially served their targets
well; it was an efficient managemeint.
(c) The World Bank projects had reached the initially set targets and inspired positively
on all aspects of and contributed much to the promotion of economic growth of rural
economy.
(i)  It had tapped new source of fund for the Spark Program and thus eased
greatly the supply of long-term fund in the projects area, and created
essential conditions for further development of Spark Program.
(ii) It enlarged the scale of industry and fostered the advantageous aggregation
of various industries in a district. A number of large scale and lucrative
enterprises were established through the selective onlending of the World
Bank loan, which emphasized on the key points of carrying big projects and
making fat profits. For examples, 8 projects had implemented at
Chongming in Shanghai since 1992, in which the average investment of a



- 75 -                   APPENDIX B
project was Y 50 million and all of them were listed in key projects locally.
In Jiangsu province, Gaoyou Brake Parts Plant, Nantong Special Steel
Works, Zhangjiagang Zhonggang Chemical Fiber Co. and Changshu
Jiangnan Synthetic Fiber Plant, Jiangyin Automobile Plates Factory,
Taixing Glass Plant, and Dantu Chemical Fiber Plant had all developed into
enterprises of over hundreds of million Renminbi sales per year or of over
profits plus tax of dozens of million Renminbi annually. All of them were
local backbone enterprises and big contributors of profit plus tax to their
governments. This indicated the vitality of the World Bank supported Spark
projects.
(iii) It raised the rural industry to a new level. Through the introduction of
foreign advanced technology and equipment, the rural industry had
acquired high technology which made technological progress not only for
the enterprise itself but also its industry sector as a whole. And, hence, the
image of the enterprises were improved. For examples, Jiangsu Yixing end-
seal Plant introduced, from Japan using the loan from the World Bank, a
cold/heat spinning machine of internationally first grade to modified the
existing forging press. It changed the backward position of 30 years behind
that of world standards, filled up the blank of this technology in China, and
become the biggest end-seal plant nationwide. Jiangsu Jingjiang Power
Machine Plant through the implementation of Spark project using
opportunity of the loan from the World Bank had developed jump-wise
from a village enterprise into a provincial level group of enterprises.
Similarly, A number of enterprises, such as Yangzhou Forge Machine
Plant, Nantong Jianghai Capacitor Plant, Zhangjiagang Dacron Filament
Plant, all had become high technology enterprises. Shanghai Chongming
Yierbao Lactic Acid Factory had developed L-lactic acid production by
high technological biotech for manufacture of products up to world
standards. This assisted the transformation of lactic acid products in China
into a new generation.
(iv) The Spark subprojects played fully the role of demonstration. The
successful subprojects supported by the World Bank had enormous
radiation capacity, acting as the center of economy in an area, diffused the
technology and products, promoted the development of similar sectors and
enterprises, and led the local corresponding industries to form the
characteristic business of their own scale. By using US$0.95 million of the
World Bank loan, Jilin Huakang Pharmacy became one of the leading
enterprises in Spark subprojects densely populated Dunhua district as well
as the mainstay Spark drugs enterprises. It acted as a group company
headed the local peasants in establishment of a multiple economic base for
Jinseng cultivation, herb drug plantation, and deer raising.



-76 -                    APPENDIX B
(v)  Siping Hongzui Steel Group jointly with Shanghai Heavy Mine Machinery
Plant and Baotou Steel Corporation, based on the introduction and
assimilation of foreign advanced technology, manufactured 4 machines of
continuous small billet caster for Zhejiang Suichang General Steel Plant
and others. It played the role of diffusion. Jiangsu Zhenjiang Bearings Plant
No. 2 had implemented a Spark subproject using the loan from the World
Bank and reached a value of production of Y 90 million and a value of
profit plus tax of Y 3.35 million in the same year when the subproject was
completed and put into operation in March of 1995. Starting from this, the
plant grew up into a core of the local economics and brought all the
enterprises in that village into a prototype aggregation of bearing
manufacturers by means of association and cooperation. In this way, a great
number of jobs were madle for the rural idle labors. There are many cases to
this. The implementation of the subprojects using the loan from the World
Bank had strengthened the connection among the enterprises and set up the
leading industries as well as brought the related rural industry along for
further development. It was these subprojects which put strongly the
formation of mainstay industries of Spark project-concentrated areas.
(vi)  The managerial supporting system of Spark Program was strengthened. The
achievements of Spark: subprojects gradually played roles in the
management of Spark Program, and improved its procedures of
administration. These inlluenced positively on the standardization and
rationalization of Spark management and thus provided necessary
conditions for further prolgress of Spark Program.
(vii) Excellent social benefits was obtained, and also the optimization and
regrouping of the rural industry structure were reached. For example, in
Jilin province the loan from the World Bank amounted as much as US$7.20
million used for the organization and regrouping of Spark projects in
combination with the key difficult issues of "How to take the advantages of
grains and to change the big agricultural province into a strong industrial
province." Thus, the technical development projects for aiding the
agricultural industry and intensely processing grains are selected. Such
subprojects included the 5 key subprojects supported by the World Bank
loan consisting of: broad agricultural film at Baicheng; organic solvents,
butanol and acetone from corn at Jiutai; and maltodextrine at Gongzhuling.
Meanwhile, high technologies were introduced in order to foster new
growing points of economiy by taking fully the advantage of the foundation
of old industries. For examples, the subproject of all plastics
telecommunication cable at Shulanwanda and broad aluminum foil of Yanji
Aluminum Industry. All of them had become the leading enterprises for
peasants to cast off poverty and get rich, firmly pushed the local industry
forward, and consequent]ly won a high reputation. The practice of Jilin
projects using the loan from the World Bank not only ended the history of



-77-                     APPENDIX B
utilization of the loan from World Bank by Jilin government being zero,
but, with their achievements and influence, also promoted the loan
application of US$120 million from the international finance organizations
for the project of comprehensive agricultural exploitation of Songliao Plain.
The significant effect of them had gone far out of the implementation of the
Spark Program itself.
(viii) A great number of managerial staff were trained. Through the stern training
of technological assessment of projects, market survey, purchase by
"Comparing offers before buying," business negotiation and so on, the
subprojects of Spark Program using the loan from the World Bank had
exploited their advantages to the full in order to educate the technical and
managerial backbone staff of the subprojects and raised the quality of the
staff of rural industry. Based on the principle of "High technology,
aggregation of enterprises, and foreign loan," the subprojects using the loan
from the World Bank took much attention to the guidance of the enterprises
for development of export oriented economy and participation in
international competition. All these had obtained superior results.
Problems
Project Management
62.   The control of projects had been concentrated on the first phase of projects
approval. STCs of all levels did not have any control on the phases of construction and
repayment of loan. This is why the feedback of progress of construction and information
concerning the production was insufficient and thus there was no solid foundation for the
controlling over the whole Program.
63.  In the past years, the managerial staff had greatly contributed and gained a great
deal of experience. However, because of that the period of inmplementation of these
projects was as long as 7 years, frequent changes of the environment, and high mobility
of the staff, the projects management were gradually weakened and did not efficiently
accumulate the managerial experience. This affected the healthy progress of the projects
and the diffusion of the achievements.
64.   The precommercial projects belong to exploratory ones. One of the criteria for
their success was the extent of transformation into commercial production. At the present
time, the rate of transformation was at a level of 50 percent. The causes of this low
percentage mainly comprise:
(a) The amount of investment become too small to complete much due to the inflation
of prices by a wide margin. One of the examples was the small investment of
US$200,000 per project at the first phase of the Program.



-78 -                    APPENDIX B
(b) Theoretically, the precommercial projects are the bridge between the scientific
research (laboratory technique or pilot experiment) and commercial production; but
the practical process of the conversion is quite complicated. Besides the technical
problems (technical cooperation, technology transformation, patent protection,
intellectual property, etc.), the major one was the capital. Capital is the vital factor
for transformation into commrercial production. If possible, to treat the
precommercial and commercial projects together as one whole project of two phases
and implement it continuously should give better result.
65.   Soft Loan Projects. The problem of this kind of projects is how to upgrade their
achievements and to make use of them efficiently.
66.   Repayment of Principle and Interest. According to the investigation and
analysis, though most of the projects operated normally, the profit of the enterprises
ubiquitously went down due to the impact of macroeconomic control, in addition to the
faint sense of the obligation of loan repayment. Therefore, they would rather use the fund
for investment in new project or for circulating capital than for repayment of the loan.
Hence, quite a number of enterprises did not fulfill the program of repayment of principle
with interest signed with the banks. A considerable number of loan were seriously over
due. The repayment of the loan from the World Bank had become a long-term challenge.
EXPERIENCES AND KEY LESSONS LEARNED
Experiences
67.  It must be emphasized that the implementation of the projects using the loan from
the World Bank is a task assigned by the government. It should have reliable supporting
conditions internally and service systemn externally. The establishment of an organization
and a system for administration of the loan from the World Bank will assure its smooth
implementation.
68.   The administration of the projects using the loan from the World Bank must be in
combination with the concrete conditions of China, and must be implemented flexibly.
Their technological content and market demand should be stressed on.
69.   The verification and evaluation of their feasibility, including market survey, the
decision of the direction of the product development, the estimation of the profits, and the
recovery rate of the investment, should be well done. This will reduce the blind
investment and raise the success rate of the projects.
70.   As to the assessment of projects, the relevant organizations should strengthen
their sense of participation, build up coordination, avoid repetitive work, and expedite the
proceeding of assessment.



- 79-                     APPENDIX B
71.   In order to speed up the implementation and construction of the projects, it is
necessary to establish a system for procuring prepayment from banks to facilitate the
system of expenditure account settlement.
72.   For the engagement of consultation firms and experts, the principles of high
quality, strict demand, and inclusion of foreigners must be observed in order to learn and
absorb the advanced management and technology from abroad.
73.   For the sake of lowering the capitalized cost, the purchase of equipment must be
accomplished through "Comparing offers before buying" and bidding.
Lessons
74.   In addition to the demanding requirements for technology and scale for the
selection of projects, it is necessary to take into account and examine strictly the credit
information, the capability of finance and management of the enterprises, the product
market as well as the qualification of the enterprise executives.
75.   The loan used to the mating projects should be fully arranged in all its aspects,
including circulating fund. The unreliability or not full payment of the fund for mating
projects are the important factor affecting the implementation of the projects, in which the
circulating fund was the very key factor for the completion, operation and profit making
of the projects. Consequently, the circulating fund should be considered one of the
components of the finance plan and entire loan used for these projects during their
finalization process.
76.   Most of the projects in China using the loans from the World Bank are long-term
and single industrial sector projects, however, the Spark project has different features:
including many short-term subprojects , many participants involving a number of sectors.
Therefore, it is necessary to constantly adapt them to the prevailing practical conditions.
77.   For those technical assistance projects longer than one year of implementation, the
terms of reference, some aspects or clauses should be supplemented or adjusted;
otherwise, it would increase the difficulty of implementation due to the unfitness of the
terms to the specific circumstances of China.

-112-                    APPENDIXB
Borrower's Comments Received from the Ministry of Science and Technology
June 26, 1998
We think the ICR on Spark Project assessed the Project reasonably and objectively
in general. The statistical tables and data are accurate.
We have some different points of view on Assessment of Outcome and Project
Sustainability for Enterprise Modernization component in Table 1- Summary of Assessment:
I1.   Assessment of Outcome for Enterprise Modernization component should be
"Satisfactory", not "Highly Unsatisfactory".
Besides objective of TA activities, the objective of Enterprise Modernization
component is accomplished in 6 years implementation: tapped new source of fund for
TVE; enlarged the scale and raised the rural industry to a new level; prompting TVE
technology progress etc. Many enterprises in the project grow up as pillar enterprises
in localities. Many examples show the project played fully the role of demonstration.
Only unsatisfactory issue- repayment - was resulted by current macroeconomics
background and legal mechanism problems in financial institutions and enterprises. It
is temporary situation and could be solved as the economic and financial reform
deepen.
2.   Project Sustainability for Enterprise Modernization component should be "Likely",
not "Uncertain".
In the view of development, the Spark subprojects satisfied the requirements of
adjustment of industry directions and the environmental policies of China. The
subprojects had high level technology. Sampling survey shows: 80% of them reached
the advanced domestic level, 19.35% were worldwide leading technology. Most of
the subprojects started from technological levels sharply more advanced than other
local industrial projects; accordingly, they possessed the ability for further
development on their own.
Most of the subprojects enterprises have good capacity to maintain their technology
level. The subprojects emphasized on new industries of materials, electronics, and
machinery It cultivated the growing points of economy. Its strategy conformed to the
trend of economic development and, therefore, increased the competitiveness in the
market. The construction scale and degree of modernization of most of the
subprojects were bigger and higher than those of the ordinary sole domestic Spark
projects.   These enterprises should have strong competitive capacity and
sustainability.
